<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Fractals_in_cell_biology">Fractals in cell biology</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fractal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Fractals in cell biology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Fractals often appear in the realm of living organisms where they arise through branching processes and other complex pattern formation. Richard Taylor and co-workers have shown that the dendritic branches of neurons form fractal patterns.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ian Wong and co-workers have shown that migrating cells can form fractals by clustering and <a href="/wiki/Branching_process" title="Branching process">branching</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neuron" title="Neuron">Nerve cells</a> function through processes at the cell surface, with phenomena that are enhanced by largely increasing the surface to volume ratio. As a consequence nerve cells often are found to form into fractal patterns.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These processes are crucial in cell <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiology</a> and different <a href="/wiki/Pathology" title="Pathology">pathologies</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Multiple subcellular structures also are found to assemble into fractals. <a href="/wiki/Diego_Krapf" title="Diego Krapf">Diego Krapf</a> has shown that through branching processes the <a href="/wiki/Actin" title="Actin">actin</a> filaments in human cells assemble into fractal patterns.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similarly Matthias Weiss showed that the <a href="/wiki/Endoplasmic_reticulum" title="Endoplasmic reticulum">endoplasmic reticulum</a> displays fractal features.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The current understanding is that fractals are ubiquitous in cell biology, from <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">proteins</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">organelles</a>, to whole cells.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="In_creative_works">In creative works</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fractal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: In creative works"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Fractal_art" title="Fractal art">Fractal art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mathematics_and_art" title="Mathematics and art">Mathematics and art</a></div>
<p><b>Fractal expressionism</b> is used to distinguish <a href="/wiki/Fractal_art" title="Fractal art">fractal art</a> generated directly by artists from fractal art generated using mathematics and/or computers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1999 numerous scientific groups have performed fractal analysis on over 50 paintings created by <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Pollock" title="Jackson Pollock">Jackson Pollock</a> by pouring paint directly onto horizontal canvasses, see for example.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-C.&#95;Redies,&#95;J&#95;2007&#95;84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C._Redies,_J_2007-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-S.&#95;Lee,&#95;S&#95;2007&#95;85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S._Lee,_S_2007-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-D.J.&#95;Field,&#95;2008&#95;87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D.J._Field,_2008-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2015, fractal analysis was used to achieve a 93% success rate in distinguishing real from imitation Pollocks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2024 study used an artificial intelligence technique based on fractals to achieve a 99% success rate.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Decalcomania" title="Decalcomania">Decalcomania</a>, a technique used by artists such as <a href="/wiki/Max_Ernst" title="Max Ernst">Max Ernst</a>, can produce fractal-like patterns.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It involves pressing paint between two surfaces and pulling them apart.
</p><p>Cyberneticist <a href="/wiki/Ron_Eglash" title="Ron Eglash">Ron Eglash</a> has suggested that fractal geometry and mathematics are prevalent in <a href="/wiki/African_art" title="African art">African art</a>, games, <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a>, trade, and architecture. Circular houses appear in circles of circles, rectangular houses in rectangles of rectangles, and so on. Such scaling patterns can also be found in African textiles, sculpture, and even cornrow hairstyles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-African&#95;art&#95;24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-African_art-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hokky_Situngkir" title="Hokky Situngkir">Hokky Situngkir</a> also suggested the similar properties in Indonesian traditional art, <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ornament_(art)" title="Ornament (art)">ornaments</a> found in traditional houses.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ethnomathematician Ron Eglash has discussed the planned layout of <a href="/wiki/Benin_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Benin city">Benin city</a> using fractals as the basis, not only in the city itself and the villages but even in the rooms of houses. He commented that "When Europeans first came to Africa, they considered the architecture very disorganised and thus primitive. It never occurred to them that the Africans might have been using a form of mathematics that they hadn't even discovered yet."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In a 1996 interview with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Silverblatt" title="Michael Silverblatt">Michael Silverblatt</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Foster_Wallace" title="David Foster Wallace">David Foster Wallace</a> explained that the structure of the first draft of <i><a href="/wiki/Infinite_Jest" title="Infinite Jest">Infinite Jest</a></i> he gave to his editor Michael Pietsch was inspired by fractals, specifically the <a href="/wiki/Sierpinski_triangle" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierpinski triangle">Sierpinski triangle</a> (a.k.a. Sierpinski gasket), but that the edited novel is "more like a lopsided Sierpinsky Gasket".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-novel&#95;23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-novel-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Some works by the Dutch artist <a href="/wiki/M._C._Escher" title="M. C. Escher">M. C. Escher</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Circle_Limit_III" title="Circle Limit III">Circle Limit III</a>, contain shapes repeated to infinity that become smaller and smaller as they get near to the edges, in a pattern that would always look the same if zoomed in.
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="fractals&#95;in&#95;technology"></span>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 259.33333333333px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 257.33333333333px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Animated_fractal_mountain.gif" class="mw-file-description" title="A fractal that models the surface of a mountain (animation)"><img alt="A fractal that models the surface of a mountain (animation)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Animated_fractal_mountain.gif/500px-Animated_fractal_mountain.gif" decoding="async" width="258" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/Animated_fractal_mountain.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="542" data-file-height="295" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">A fractal that models the surface of a mountain (animation)</div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 188.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 186.66666666667px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:FRACTAL-3d-FLOWER.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="3D recursive image"><img alt="3D recursive image" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/FRACTAL-3d-FLOWER.jpg/330px-FRACTAL-3d-FLOWER.jpg" decoding="async" width="187" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/FRACTAL-3d-FLOWER.jpg/500px-FRACTAL-3d-FLOWER.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/FRACTAL-3d-FLOWER.jpg/640px-FRACTAL-3d-FLOWER.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></span></div>

		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 188.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 186.66666666667px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Fractal-BUTTERFLY.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Recursive fractal butterfly image"><img alt="Recursive fractal butterfly image" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Fractal-BUTTERFLY.jpg/330px-Fractal-BUTTERFLY.jpg" decoding="async" width="187" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Fractal-BUTTERFLY.jpg/500px-Fractal-BUTTERFLY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Fractal-BUTTERFLY.jpg/640px-Fractal-BUTTERFLY.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">Recursive fractal butterfly image</div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 188.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 186.66666666667px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Apophysis-100303-104.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="A fractal flame"><img alt="A fractal flame" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Apophysis-100303-104.jpg/330px-Apophysis-100303-104.jpg" decoding="async" width="187" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Apophysis-100303-104.jpg/500px-Apophysis-100303-104.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Apophysis-100303-104.jpg/960px-Apophysis-100303-104.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">A <a href="/wiki/Fractal_flame" title="Fractal flame">fractal flame</a></div>
		</li>
</ul>
<p>Biophilic fractals are patterns designed to induce the health and well-being benefits associated with exposure to nature's scenery.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These include stress-reduction and enhanced cognitive capacity. Designers and architects incorporate biophilic fractals into the built environment to counter the fact that people spend 92% of their time indoors and away from nature's scenery. The Fractal Chapel designed by INNOCAD architecture at the University Hospital in Graz, Austria, is a prominent example and recipient of both the IIDA (International Interior Design Association) Best of Competition 2025 Award and the World Interior of the Year 2025 Award at the World Architecture Festival (WAF).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Physiological_responses:_Fractal_Fluency">Physiological responses: Fractal Fluency</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fractal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Physiological responses: Fractal Fluency"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Fractal fluency is a <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> model that proposes that, through exposure to nature's fractal scenery, people's <a href="/wiki/Visual_system" title="Visual system">visual systems</a> have adapted to efficiently process fractals with ease. This adaptation occurs at many stages of the visual system, from the way people's eyes move to which regions of the brain get activated.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Fluency puts the viewer in a 'comfort zone' so inducing an aesthetic experience. Neuroscience experiments have shown that Jackson Pollock's fractal paintings induce the same positive <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiological</a> responses in the observer as nature's fractals and mathematical fractals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-R.P.&#95;Taylor,&#95;B.&#95;Spehar&#95;2011&#95;104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R.P._Taylor,_B._Spehar_2011-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This shows that fractal expressionism is related to fractal fluency by providing motivation for artists, such as Pollock, to use Fractal Expressionism in their art to appeal to people.
</p><p>Humans appear to be especially well-adapted to processing fractal patterns with <a href="/wiki/Fractal_dimension" title="Fractal dimension">fractal dimension</a> between 1.3 and 1.5.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When humans view fractal patterns with fractal dimensions in this range, these fractals reduce physiological stress and boost cognitive abilities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Taylor&#95;2006&#95;106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor_2006-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Applications_in_technology">Applications in technology</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fractal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Applications in technology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fractal_analysis" title="Fractal analysis">Fractal analysis</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1184024115" /><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 25em;">
<ul><li>Fractal Bionics<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fractal_antenna" title="Fractal antenna">Fractal antennas</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-antenna&#95;108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-antenna-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Fractal transistor<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fractal&#95;transistor&#95;109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fractal_transistor-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Fractal heat exchangers<sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>

The topological dimension and Hausdorff dimension of the image of the Hilbert map in <b>R</b><sup>2</sup> are both 2. Note, however, that the topological dimension of the <i>graph</i> of the Hilbert map (a set in <b>R</b><sup>3</sup>) is 1.</span>
